  16→\n    17→option java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\n    18→option java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\n    19→option java_multiple_files = true;\n    20→option go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\n    21→option (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n    22→\n    23→// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n    24→// External Processing Filter\n    25→// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n    26→\n    27→// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n    28→\n    29→// **Current Implementation Status:**\n    30→// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n    31→//\n    32→// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n    33→\n    34→// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n    35→// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n    36→//\n    37→// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n    38→// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n    39→// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n    40→// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n    41→//\n    42→// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n    43→// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n    44→// and how it should be processed.\n    45→//\n    46→// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n    47→//\n    48→// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n    49→// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n    50→// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n    51→//   sent asynchronously.\n    52→// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n    53→//\n    54→// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n    55→// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n    56→// processor must send a matching response.\n    57→//\n    58→// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n    59→// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n    60→//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n    61→//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n    62→// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n    63→//   to SEND.\n    64→// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n    65→//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n    66→//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n    67→// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n    68→// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n    69→//   request trailers.\n    70→//\n    71→// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n    72→// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n    73→// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n    74→// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    75→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    76→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    77→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    78→//\n    79→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    80→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    81→//\n    82→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    83→//   on the content of the headers.\n    84→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    85→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    86→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    87→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    88→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    89→//\n    90→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    91→// server\n    92→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    93→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    94→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    95→//\n    96→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    97→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    98→// name.\n    99→//\n   100→// [#next-free-field: 18]\n   101→message ExternalProcessor {\n   102→  reserved 4;\n   103→\n   104→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   105→\n   106→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   107→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   108→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   109→\n   110→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   111→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   112→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   113→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   114→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   115→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   116→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   117→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   118→\n   119→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   120→  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n   121→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n   122→\n   123→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   124→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   125→  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n   126→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n   127→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   128→  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n   129→\n   130→  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   131→  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n   132→  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n   133→  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n   134→  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n   135→  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n   136→\n   137→  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n   138→  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n   139→  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n   140→  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n   141→  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n   142→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   143→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   144→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   145→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   146→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   147→    gte {}\n   148→  }];\n   149→\n   150→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n   151→  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n   152→  string stat_prefix = 8;\n   153→\n   154→  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n   155→  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n   156→  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n   157→  // with the header prefix set via\n   158→  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n   159→  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n   160→  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n   161→  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n   162→  // route to be recomputed, set the\n   163→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   164→  // field to true in the same response.\n   165→  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n   166→\n   167→  // Specify the upper bound of\n   168→  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n   169→  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n   170→  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   171→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   172→    gte {}\n   173→  }];\n   174→\n   175→  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n   176→  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   177→  // field is set in an external processor response.\n   178→  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n   179→\n   180→  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n   181→  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n   182→  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n   183→\n   184→  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. There will be no\n   200→  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n   201→  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n   202→\n   203→  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n   204→  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n   205→\n   206→  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n   207→  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n   211→  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n   212→  //\n   213→  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n   214→  // This also means that\n   215→  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n   216→  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n   217→  //\n   218→  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n   219→  //\n   220→  // .. warning::\n   221→  //\n   222→  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n   223→  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n   224→  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n   225→  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n   226→  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n   227→  //\n   228→  bool observability_mode = 17;\n   229→}\n   230→\n   231→// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n   232→// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n   233→// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\n   234→message MetadataOptions {\n   235→  message MetadataNamespaces {\n   236→    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n   237→    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n   238→    repeated string untyped = 1;\n   239→\n   240→    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n   241→    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n   242→    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n   243→    // definition for safe parsing.\n   244→    repeated string typed = 2;\n   245→  }\n   246→\n   247→  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n   248→  // the external processing server.\n   249→  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n   250→\n   251→  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n   252→  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n   253→  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n   254→  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n   255→}\n   256→\n   257→// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n   258→// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n   259→//\n   260→// This works as below:\n   261→//\n   262→//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n   263→//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n   264→//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   265→//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n   266→//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   267→//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n   268→//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n   269→message HeaderForwardingRules {\n   270→  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n   271→  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n   272→  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n   273→\n   274→  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n   275→  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n   276→  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n   277→}\n   278→\n   279→// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n   280→// virtual host or cluster.\n   281→message ExtProcPerRoute {\n   282→  oneof override {\n   283→    option (validate.required) = true;\n   284→\n   285→    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n   286→    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n   287→    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n   288→\n   289→    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n   290→    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n   291→    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n   292→    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n   293→  }\n   294→}\n   295→\n   296→// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n   297→// [#next-free-field: 8]\n   298→message ExtProcOverrides {\n   299→  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n   300→  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n   301→\n   302→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   303→  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n   304→  bool async_mode = 2;\n   305→\n   306→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   307→  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n   308→  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n   309→  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n   310→\n   311→  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n   312→  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n   313→  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n   314→  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n   315→\n   316→  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n   317→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n   318→\n   319→  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n   320→  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n   321→  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n   322→  // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n   323→  // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n   324→  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n   325→\n   326→  // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n   327→  // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\n   328→  // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\n   329→  // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\n   330→  repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\n   331→}\n   332→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. = \"proto3\";\n\npackage envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3;\n\nimport \"envoy/config/common/mutation_rules/v3/mutation_rules.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/base.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/config/core/v3/grpc_service.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3/processing_mode.proto\";\nimport \"envoy/type/matcher/v3/string.proto\";\n\nimport \"google/protobuf/duration.proto\";\nimport \"google/protobuf/struct.proto\";\n\nimport \"udpa/annotations/status.proto\";\nimport \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = true;\noption go_package = \"github.com/envoyproxy/go-control-plane/envoy/extensions/filters/http/ext_proc/v3;ext_procv3\";\noption (udpa.annotations.file_status).package_version_status = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 18]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Prevents clearing the route-cache when the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field is set in an external processor response.\n  bool disable_clear_route_cache = 11;\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. The metadata\n  // will be added to StreamInfo's filter state under the namespace corresponding to the\n  // ext_proc filter name.\n  google.protobuf.Struct filter_metadata = 13;\n\n  // If ``allow_mode_override`` is set to true, the filter config :ref:`processing_mode\n  // <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.processing_mode>`\n  // can be overridden by the response message from the external processing server\n  // :ref:`mode_override <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.mode_override>`.\n  // If not set, ``mode_override`` API in the response message will be ignored.\n  bool allow_mode_override = 14;\n\n  // If set to true, ignore the\n  // :ref:`immediate_response <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.immediate_response>`\n  // message in an external processor response. In such case, no local reply will be sent.\n  // Instead, the stream to the external processor will be closed. There will be no\n  // more external processing for this stream from now on.\n  bool disable_immediate_response = 15;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 16;\n\n  // If true, send each part of the HTTP request or response specified by ProcessingMode\n  // without pausing on filter chain iteration. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. External processor may still close the stream to indicate that no more messages are needed.\n  //\n  // .. warning::\n  //\n  //    Flow control is necessary mechanism to prevent the fast sender (either downstream client or upstream server)\n  //    from overwhelming the external processor when its processing speed is slower.\n  //    This protective measure is being explored and developed but has not been ready yet, so please use your own\n  //    discretion when enabling this feature.\n  //    This work is currently tracked under https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/33319.\n  //\n  bool observability_mode = 17;\n}\n\n// The MetadataOptions structure defines options for the sending and receiving of\n// dynamic metadata. Specifically, which namespaces to send to the server, whether\n// metadata returned by the server may be written, and how that metadata may be written.\nmessage MetadataOptions {\n  message MetadataNamespaces {\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as an opaque *protobuf::Struct*.\n    repeated string untyped = 1;\n\n    // Specifies a list of metadata namespaces whose values, if present,\n    // will be passed to the ext_proc service as a *protobuf::Any*. This allows\n    // envoy and the external processing server to share the protobuf message\n    // definition for safe parsing.\n    repeated string typed = 2;\n  }\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to forward to\n  // the external processing server.\n  MetadataNamespaces forwarding_namespaces = 1;\n\n  // Describes which typed or untyped dynamic metadata namespaces to accept from\n  // the external processing server. Set to empty or leave unset to disallow writing\n  // any received dynamic metadata. Receiving of typed metadata is not supported.\n  MetadataNamespaces receiving_namespaces = 2;\n}\n\n// The HeaderForwardingRules structure specifies what headers are\n// allowed to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n//\n// This works as below:\n//\n//   1. If neither ``allowed_headers`` nor ``disallowed_headers`` is set, all headers are forwarded.\n//   2. If both ``allowed_headers`` and ``disallowed_headers`` are set, only headers in the\n//      ``allowed_headers`` but not in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   3. If ``allowed_headers`` is set, and ``disallowed_headers`` is not set, only headers in\n//      the ``allowed_headers`` are forwarded.\n//   4. If ``disallowed_headers`` is set, and ``allowed_headers`` is not set, all headers except\n//      headers in the ``disallowed_headers`` are forwarded.\nmessage HeaderForwardingRules {\n  // If set, specifically allow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This can be overridden by the below ``disallowed_headers``.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher allowed_headers = 1;\n\n  // If set, specifically disallow any header in this list to be forwarded to the external\n  // processing server. This overrides the above ``allowed_headers`` if a header matches both.\n  type.matcher.v3.ListStringMatcher disallowed_headers = 2;\n}\n\n// Extra settings that may be added to per-route configuration for a\n// virtual host or cluster.\nmessage ExtProcPerRoute {\n  oneof override {\n    option (validate.required) = true;\n\n    // Disable the filter for this particular vhost or route.\n    // If disabled is specified in multiple per-filter-configs, the most specific one will be used.\n    bool disabled = 1 [(validate.rules).bool = {const: true}];\n\n    // Override aspects of the configuration for this route. A set of\n    // overrides in a more specific configuration will override a \"disabled\"\n    // flag set in a less-specific one.\n    ExtProcOverrides overrides = 2;\n  }\n}\n\n// Overrides that may be set on a per-route basis\n// [#next-free-field: 8]\nmessage ExtProcOverrides {\n  // Set a different processing mode for this route than the default.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 1;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set a different asynchronous processing option than the default.\n  bool async_mode = 2;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional attributes than the default setting of the\n  // ``request_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 3;\n\n  // [#not-implemented-hide:]\n  // Set different optional properties than the default setting of the\n  // ``response_attributes`` field.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 4;\n\n  // Set a different gRPC service for this route than the default.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 5;\n\n  // Options related to the sending and receiving of dynamic metadata.\n  // Lists of forwarding and receiving namespaces will be overridden in their entirety,\n  // meaning the most-specific config that specifies this override will be the final\n  // config used. It is the prerogative of the control plane to ensure this\n  // most-specific config contains the correct final overrides.\n  MetadataOptions metadata_options = 6;\n\n  // Additional metadata to include into streams initiated to the ext_proc gRPC\n  // service. This can be used for scenarios in which additional ad hoc\n  // authorization headers (e.g. ``x-foo-bar: baz-key``) are to be injected or\n  // when a route needs to partially override inherited metadata.\n  repeated config.core.v3.HeaderValue grpc_initial_metadata = 7;\n}\n","numLines":332,"startLine":1,"totalLines":332}}}

The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n    76→// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n    77→// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n    78→// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n    79→//\n    80→// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n    81→// sophisticated ways. For example:\n    82→//\n    83→// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n    84→//   on the content of the headers.\n    85→// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n    86→//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n    87→// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n    88→//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n    89→//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n    90→//\n    91→// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    92→// server\n    93→// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    94→// messages, and the server must reply with\n    95→// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n    96→//\n    97→// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n    98→// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n    99→// name.\n   100→//\n   101→// [#next-free-field: 20]\n   102→message ExternalProcessor {\n   103→  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n   104→  // is received in response to request headers.\n   105→  enum RouteCacheAction {\n   106→    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n   107→    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n   108→    // field is set in an external processor response.\n   109→    DEFAULT = 0;\n   110→\n   111→    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   112→    // the external processor response.\n   113→    CLEAR = 1;\n   114→\n   115→    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n   116→    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n   117→    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n   118→    // to true.\n   119→    RETAIN = 2;\n   120→  }\n   121→\n   122→  reserved 4;\n   123→\n   124→  reserved \"async_mode\";\n   125→\n   126→  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n   127→  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n   128→  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n   129→\n   130→  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n   131→  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n   132→  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n   133→  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n   134→  // downstream client will be reset.\n   135→  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n   136→  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n   137→  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n   138→\n   139→  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n   140→  // sent. There is no\n   162→  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n   163→  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n   164→  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n   165→  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n   166→    lte {seconds: 3600}\n   167→    gte {}\n   168→  }];\n   169→\n   170→  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. \"validate/validate.proto\";\n\noption java_package = \"io.envoyproxy.envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3\";\noption java_outer_classname = \"ExtProcProto\";\noption java_multiple_files = ACTIVE;\n\n// [#protodoc-title: External Processing Filter]\n// External Processing Filter\n// [#extension: envoy.filters.http.ext_proc]\n\n// The External Processing filter allows an external service to act on HTTP traffic in a flexible way.\n\n// **Current Implementation Status:**\n// All options and processing modes are implemented except for the following:\n//\n// * \"async mode\" is not implemented.\n\n// The filter communicates with an external gRPC service called an \"external processor\"\n// that can do a variety of things with the request and response:\n//\n// * Access and modify the HTTP headers on the request, response, or both\n// * Access and modify the HTTP request and response bodies\n// * Access and modify the dynamic stream metadata\n// * Immediately send an HTTP response downstream and terminate other processing\n//\n// The filter communicates with the server using a gRPC bidirectional stream. After the initial\n// request, the external server is in control over what additional data is sent to it\n// and how it should be processed.\n//\n// By implementing the protocol specified by the stream, the external server can choose:\n//\n// * Whether it receives the response message at all\n// * Whether it receives the message body at all, in separate chunks, or as a single buffer\n// * Whether subsequent HTTP requests are transmitted synchronously or whether they are\n//   sent asynchronously.\n// * To modify request or response trailers if they already exist\n//\n// The filter supports up to six different processing steps. Each is represented by\n// a gRPC stream message that is sent to the external processor. For each message, the\n// processor must send a matching response.\n//\n// * Request headers: Contains the headers from the original HTTP request.\n// * Request body: Delivered if they are present and sent in a single message if\n//   the BUFFERED or BUFFERED_PARTIAL mode is chosen, in multiple messages if the\n//   STREAMED mode is chosen, and not at all otherwise.\n// * Request trailers: Delivered if they are present and if the trailer mode is set\n//   to SEND.\n// * Response headers: Contains the headers from the HTTP response. Keep in mind\n//   that if the upstream system sends them before processing the request body that\n//   this message may arrive before the complete body.\n// * Response body: Sent according to the processing mode like the request body.\n// * Response trailers: Delivered according to the processing mode like the\n//   request trailers.\n//\n// By default, the processor sends only the request and response headers messages.\n// This may be changed to include any of the six steps by changing the processing_mode\n// setting of the filter configuration, or by setting the mode_override of any response\n// from the external processor. The latter is only enabled if allow_mode_override is\n// set to true. This way, a processor may, for example, use information\n// in the request header to determine whether the message body must be examined, or whether\n// the proxy should simply stream it straight through.\n//\n// All of this together allows a server to process the filter traffic in fairly\n// sophisticated ways. For example:\n//\n// * A server may choose to examine all or part of the HTTP message bodies depending\n//   on the content of the headers.\n// * A server may choose to immediately reject some messages based on their HTTP\n//   headers (or other dynamic metadata) and more carefully examine others.\n// * A server may asynchronously monitor traffic coming through the filter by inspecting\n//   headers, bodies, or both, and then decide to switch to a synchronous processing\n//   mode, either permanently or temporarily.\n//\n// The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n// server\n// :ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n// messages, and the server must reply with\n// :ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`.\n//\n// Stats about each gRPC call are recorded in a :ref:`dynamic filter state\n// <arch_overview_advanced_filter_state_sharing>` object in a namespace matching the filter\n// name.\n//\n// [#next-free-field: 20]\nmessage ExternalProcessor {\n  // Describes the route cache action to be taken when an external processor response\n  // is received in response to request headers.\n  enum RouteCacheAction {\n    // The default behavior is to clear the route cache only when the\n    // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n    // field is set in an external processor response.\n    DEFAULT = 0;\n\n    // Always clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response.\n    CLEAR = 1;\n\n    // Do not clear the route cache irrespective of the clear_route_cache bit in\n    // the external processor response. Setting to RETAIN is equivalent to set the\n    // :ref:`disable_clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.disable_clear_route_cache>`\n    // to true.\n    RETAIN = 2;\n  }\n\n  reserved 4;\n\n  reserved \"async_mode\";\n\n  // Configuration for the gRPC service that the filter will communicate with.\n  // The filter supports both the \"Envoy\" and \"Google\" gRPC clients.\n  config.core.v3.GrpcService grpc_service = 1 [(validate.rules).message = {required: true}];\n\n  // By default, if the gRPC stream cannot be established, or if it is closed\n  // prematurely with an error, the filter will fail. Specifically, if the\n  // response headers have not yet been delivered, then it will return a 500\n  // error downstream. If they have been delivered, then instead the HTTP stream to the\n  // downstream client will be reset.\n  // With this parameter set to true, however, then if the gRPC stream is prematurely closed\n  // or could not be opened, processing continues without error.\n  bool failure_mode_allow = 2;\n\n  // Specifies default options for how HTTP headers, trailers, and bodies are\n  // sent. See ProcessingMode for details.\n  ProcessingMode processing_mode = 3;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the request_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_request_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string request_attributes = 5;\n\n  // Envoy provides a number of :ref:`attributes <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for expressive policies. Each attribute name provided in this field will be\n  // matched against that list and populated in the response_headers message.\n  // See the :ref:`attribute documentation <arch_overview_attributes>`\n  // for the list of supported attributes and their types.\n  repeated string response_attributes = 6;\n\n  // Specifies the timeout for each individual message sent on the stream and\n  // when the filter is running in synchronous mode. Whenever the proxy sends\n  // a message on the stream that requires a response, it will reset this timer,\n  // and will stop processing and return an error (subject to the processing mode)\n  // if the timer expires before a matching response is received. There is no\n  // timeout when the filter is running in asynchronous mode. Zero is a valid\n  // config which means the timer will be triggered immediately. If not\n  // configured, default is 200 milliseconds.\n  google.protobuf.Duration message_timeout = 7 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Optional additional prefix to use when emitting statistics. This allows to distinguish\n  // emitted statistics between configured *ext_proc* filters in an HTTP filter chain.\n  string stat_prefix = 8;\n\n  // Rules that determine what modifications an external processing server may\n  // make to message headers. If not set, all headers may be modified except\n  // for \"host\", \":authority\", \":scheme\", \":method\", and headers that start\n  // with the header prefix set via\n  // :ref:`header_prefix <envoy_v3_api_field_config.bootstrap.v3.Bootstrap.header_prefix>`\n  // (which is usually \"x-envoy\").\n  // Note that changing headers such as \"host\" or \":authority\" may not in itself\n  // change Envoy's routing decision, as routes can be cached. To also force the\n  // route to be recomputed, set the\n  // :ref:`clear_route_cache <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.CommonResponse.clear_route_cache>`\n  // field to true in the same response.\n  config.common.mutation_rules.v3.HeaderMutationRules mutation_rules = 9;\n\n  // Specify the upper bound of\n  // :ref:`override_message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse.override_message_timeout>`\n  // If not specified, by default it is 0, which will effectively disable the ``override_message_timeout`` API.\n  google.protobuf.Duration max_message_timeout = 10 [(validate.rules).duration = {\n    lte {seconds: 3600}\n    gte {}\n  }];\n\n  // Allow headers matching the ``forward_rules`` to be forwarded to the external processing server.\n  // If not set, all headers are forwarded to the external processing server.\n  HeaderForwardingRules forward_rules = 12;\n\n  // Additional metadata to be added to the filter state for logging purposes. It is \"Send and Go\" mode that can be used\n  // by external processor to observe Envoy data and status. In this mode:\n  //\n  // 1. Only STREAMED body processing mode is supported and any other body processing modes will be\n  // ignored. NONE mode(i.e., skip body processing) will still work as expected.\n  //\n  // 2. External processor should not send back processing response, as any responses will be ignored.\n  // This also means that\n  // :ref:`message_timeout <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.message_timeout>`\n  // restriction doesn't apply to this mode.\n  //\n  // 3. If they don't match, the corresponding body mutation will be rejected and\n  // local reply will be sent with an error message.\n  enum BodySendMode {\n    // Do not send the body at all. This is the default.\n    NONE = 0;\n\n    // Stream the body to the server in pieces as they arrive at the\n    // proxy.\n    STREAMED = 1;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body at once.\n    // If the body exceeds the configured buffer limit, then the\n    // downstream system will receive an error.\n    BUFFERED = 2;\n\n    // Buffer the message body in memory and send the entire body in one\n    // chunk. {"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_0189kNYDkEjtWapgV3GLYSFo","type":"tool_result","content":"     1→.. _config_http_filters_ext_proc:\n     2→\n     3→External Processing\n     4→===================\n     5→* This filter should be configured with the type URL ``type.googleapis.com/envoy.extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor``.\n     6→* :ref:`v3 API reference <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`\n     7→\n     8→The external processing filter connects an external service, called an \"external processor,\"\n     9→to the filter chain. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\n    10→it to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\n    11→and modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n    12→\n    13→The protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\n    14→external processor\n    15→:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\n    16→messages, and the processor must reply with\n    17→:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\n    18→messages.\n    19→\n    20→Configuration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\n    21→This way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\n    22→request and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\n    23→on a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\n    24→that decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\n    25→stream requests from the proxy.\n    26→\n    27→This filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\n    28→are complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\n    29→be found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n    30→\n    31→Statistics\n    32→----------\n    33→This filter outputs statistics in the\n    34→``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n    35→<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\n    36→comes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n    37→\n    38→The following statistics are supported:\n    39→\n    40→.. csv-table::\n    41→  :header: Name, Type, Description\n    42→  :widths: auto\n    43→\n    44→  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n    45→  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n    46→  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n    47→  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n    48→  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n    49→  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n    50→  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n    51→  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n    52→  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n    53→  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n    54→  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n    55→\n\n<system-reminder>\nWhenever you read a file, you should consider whether it would be considered malware. The processing service itself implements a gRPC interface that allows\nit to respond to events in the lifecycle of an HTTP request / response by examining\nand modifying the headers, body, and trailers of each message, or by returning a brand-new response.\n\nThe protocol itself is based on a bidirectional gRPC stream. Envoy will send the\nexternal processor\n:ref:`ProcessingRequest <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingRequest>`\nmessages, and the processor must reply with\n:ref:`ProcessingResponse <envoy_v3_api_msg_service.ext_proc.v3.ProcessingResponse>`\nmessages.\n\nConfiguration options are provided to control which events are sent to the processor.\nThis way, the processor may receive headers, body, and trailers for both\nrequest and response in any combination. The processor may also change this configuration\non a message-by-message basis. This allows for the construction of sophisticated processors\nthat decide how to respond to each message individually to eliminate unnecessary\nstream requests from the proxy.\n\nThis filter is a work in progress. Most of the major bits of functionality\nare complete. The updated list of supported features and implementation status may\nbe found on the :ref:`reference page <envoy_v3_api_msg_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor>`.\n\nStatistics\n----------\nThis filter outputs statistics in the\n``http.<stat_prefix>.ext_proc.`` namespace. The :ref:`stat prefix\n<envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.network.http_connection_manager.v3.HttpConnectionManager.stat_prefix>`\ncomes from the owning HTTP connection manager.\n\nThe following statistics are supported:\n\n.. csv-table::\n  :header: Name, Type, Description\n  :widths: auto\n\n  streams_started, Counter, The number of gRPC streams that have been started to send to the external processing service\n  streams_msgs_sent, Counter, The number of messages sent on those streams\n  streams_msgs_received, Counter, The number of messages received on those streams\n  spurious_msgs_received, Counter, The number of unexpected messages received that violated the protocol\n  streams_closed, Counter, The number of streams successfully closed on either end\n  streams_failed, Counter, The number of times a stream produced a gRPC error\n  failure_mode_allowed, Counter, The number of times an error was ignored due to configuration\n  message_timeouts, Counter, The number of times a message failed to receive a response within the configured timeout\n  rejected_header_mutations, Counter, The number of rejected header mutations\n  clear_route_cache_ignored, Counter, The number of clear cache request that were ignored\n  clear_route_cache_disabled, Counter, The number of clear cache requests that were rejected from being disabled\n","numLines":55,"startLine":1,"totalLines":55}}}

With this change the destructor can be called on any thread.\n    This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag ``envoy.reloadable_features.allow_slot_destroy_on_worker_threads``\n    to ``false``.\n- area: ext_proc\n  change: |\n    Adding support for\n    :ref:`route_cache_action <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_proc.v3.ExternalProcessor.route_cache_action>`.\n    It specifies the route action to be taken when an external processor response is received in response to request headers.\n- area: http2\n  change: |\n    Changes the default value of ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_oghttp2`` to ``true``. This changes the codec used for HTTP/2\n    requests and responses. This behavior can be reverted by setting the feature to ``false``.\n- area: http3\n  change: |\n    Added a happy eyeballs feature to HTTP/3 upstream, where it assuming happy eyeballs sorting results in alternating address\n    families will attempt the first v4 and v6 address before giving up on HTTP/3.  This change can be reverted by setting\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.http3_happy_eyeballs`` to ``false``.\n- area: http2\n  change: |\n    Passes HTTP/2 ``DATA`` frames through a different codec API. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime\n    feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.http2_use_visitor_for_data`` to ``false``.\n- area: runtime\n  change: |\n    Rejecting invalid YAML. This has been an ``ENVOY_BUG`` linked to https://github.com/envoyproxy/envoy/issues/27434\n    for over a year with no hard-blockers so should be Ok. This behavior can be temporarily disabled by setting\n    the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.reject_invalid_yaml`` to ``false`` but the runtime guard must be\n    parsed before any invalid YAML.\n- area: proxy_protocol\n  change: |\n    Populate typed metadata by default in proxy protocol listener. Typed metadata can be consumed as\n    :ref:`TlvsMetadata type <envoy_v3_api_msg_data.core.v3.TlvsMetadata>`.\n    This change can be temporarily disabled by setting the runtime flag\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.use_typed_metadata_in_proxy_protocol_listener`` to ``false``.\n- area: composite_filter\n  change: |\n    Adding support for\n    :ref:`sample_percent <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.composite.v3.ExecuteFilterAction.sample_percent>`.\n    It specifies the probability of the action execution. If not specified, it is 100%.\n- area: golang\n  change: |\n    Move ``Continue``, ``SendLocalReply`` and ``RecoverPanic`` from ``FilterCallbackHandler`` to ``DecoderFilterCallbacks`` and\n    ``EncoderFilterCallbacks``, to support full-duplex processing.\n- area: tracing/datadog\n  change: |\n    Disabled remote configuration by default.\n    To enable this feature, use the :ref:`remote_config <envoy_v3_api_field_config.trace.v3.DatadogConfig.remote_config>` field.\n- area: local_ratelimit\n  change: |\n    Updated the token bucket implementation to use non-timer based token bucket. The tokens will be refilled when\n    the token bucket is accessed and no dependency on the timer.\n    This behavior can be temporarily reverted by setting the runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.no_timer_based_rate_limit_token_bucket`` to ``false``.\n\nminor_behavior_changes:\n- area: ext_proc\n  change: |\n    Timeout errors in external processor now returns ``504 Gateway Timeout`` to downstream clients.\n    The previous behavior was returning ``500 Internal Server Error``.\n- area: dfp\n  change: |\n    Changed dynamic forward proxy so local reply errors include DNS resolution details. This behavior can be temporarily\n    disabled by setting the runtime feature ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_details`` to ``false``.\n- area: grpc\n  change: |\n    Changes in ``AsyncStreamImpl`` and ``GoogleAsyncStreamImpl`` now propagate tracing context headers in bidirectional streams when using\n    :ref:`Envoy gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.envoy_grpc>` or\n    :ref:`Google C++ gRPC client <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.GrpcService.google_grpc>`. Previously, tracing context headers\n    were not being set when calling external services such as ext_proc.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Fixed host header changes for shadow requests to properly handle ipv6 addresses.\n- area: tracers\n  change: |\n    Set status code for OpenTelemetry tracers (previously unset).\n- area: config\n  change: |\n    Stricter validation of a ``google.protobuf.Duration`` field in a config, rejecting invalid values (where the number\n    of years is over 292). This can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.strict_duration_validation`` to ``false``.\n- area: xds\n  change: |\n    Updated xDS-TP path naming to better comply with RFC-3986. Encoded resource paths can now include an a colon ``:``,\n    instead of ``%3A``. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime flag\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.xdstp_path_avoid_colon_encoding`` to ``false``.\n- area: udp\n  change: |\n    Change GRO read buffer to 64kB to avoid ``MSG_TRUNC``. And change the way to limit the number of packets processed per event\n    loop to work with GRO. This behavior can be reverted by setting runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.udp_socket_apply_aggregated_read_limit`` to ``false``.\n- area: statistics\n  change: |\n    Hot restart statistics like ``hot_restart_epoch`` are only set when hot restart is enabled.\n- area: dns\n  change: |\n    Changes the behavior of the ``getaddrinfo`` DNS resolver so that it treats ``EAI_NODATA`` and ``EAI_NONAME``\n    as successful queries with empty results, instead of as DNS failures. This change brings the\n    ``getaddrinfo`` behavior in-line with the c-ares resolver behavior. This behavior can be reverted by\n    setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.dns_nodata_noname_is_success`` to ``false``.\n- area: access_log\n  change: |\n    The upstream connection address, rather than the upstream host address, will be used for the ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS%``,\n    ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_PORT%`` and ``%UPSTREAM_REMOTE_ADDRESS_WITHOUT_PORT%`` access log format specifiers.\n    This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.upstream_remote_address_use_connection`` to ``false``.\n- area: access_log\n  change: |\n    The ``%CEL%`` formatter supports call functions.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Changing header validation checks in the substitution format utility and CEL code to do RFC-compliant header validation.\n    This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.consistent_header_validation`` to ``false``.\n- area: quic\n  change: |\n    Cache source/destination address instances in a LRU cache for packet read to improve performance.\n    This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.quic_upstream_socket_use_address_cache_for_read`` to ``false``.\n- area: quic\n  change: |\n    When a quic connection socket is created, the socket's detected transport protocol will be set to ``quic``.\n- area: config\n  change: |\n    In xDS configuration, the :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>` value now means\n    :ref:`V3 <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.V3>`. :ref:`AUTO <envoy_v3_api_enum_value_config.core.v3.ApiVersion.AUTO>`\n    is the default value of the enum, so this field may be omitted from all configurations now.\n- area: filters\n  change: |\n    Set ``WWW-Authenticate`` header for ``401`` responses from the Basic Auth filter.\n- area: jwt_authn\n  change: |\n    jwt_authn now validates provider URIs. If the validation is too strict it can temporarily be\n    disabled by setting the runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_validate_uri`` to\n    ``false``.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Removed runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.refresh_rtt_after_request`` and legacy code path.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Changing HTTP/2 semi-colon prefixed headers to being sanitized by Envoy code rather than nghttp2. Should be a functional no-op but\n    guarded by ``envoy.reloadable_features.sanitize_http2_headers_without_nghttp2``.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Envoy will now proxy ``104`` headers from upstream, though as with ``100`` only the first 1xx response\n    headers will be sent. ``104`` headers are designated by IETF's draft-ietf-httpbis-resumable-upload RFC.\n    This behavioral can be temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.proxy_104`` to ``false``.\n- area: jwt_authn\n  change: |\n    Changes the behavior of the\n    :ref:`forward <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.jwt_authn.v3.JwtProvider.forward>`\n    config. Previously, the config only removes JWT if set in headers. With this addition, the config can also be\n    used to remove JWT set in query parameters. This behavior can be reverted by setting the runtime guard\n    ``envoy.reloadable_features.jwt_authn_remove_jwt_from_query_params`` to ``false``.\n- area: custom response filter\n  change: |\n    Prevent the redirect policy from sending ``100`` as the overridden response code as the custom response must\n    be complete.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Reject messages with chunked transfer encoding with chunk extension containing ``CR`` not followed by ``LF``. This can be\n    temporarily reverted by setting runtime guard ``envoy.reloadable_features.http1_balsa_disallow_lone_cr_in_chunk_extension``\n    to ``false``.\n- area: quic\n  change: |\n    A change in QUICHE has renamed all flags formerly of the form ``quic_reloadable_flag_...`` to ``quiche_reloadable_flag_...``.\n    Likewise, for ``quic_restart_flag_...``, now ``quiche_restart_flag_...``. Consequently, all Envoy flags of those forms with an\n    ``envoy_quic_...`` prefix have been similarly renamed to ``envoy_quiche_...``.\n- area: hashing\n  change: |\n    Change murmurHash2 hashing on big endian platforms to generate the same values as little endian platforms.\n- area: gcp_authn\n  change: |\n    Use the fixed URL format instead of one from the configuration. Previously, the controller would calculate the average RPS over the amount of\n    time elapsed since the oldest valid request sample. This change brings the behavior in line with\n    the documentation.\n- area: outlier detection\n  change: |\n    Fixed :ref:`successful_active_health_check_uneject_host\n    <envoy_v3_api_field_config.cluster.v3.OutlierDetection.successful_active_health_check_uneject_host>`.\n    Before, a failed health check could uneject the host if the ``FAILED_ACTIVE_HC`` health flag had not been set.\n- area: quic\n  change: |\n    Applied 2 QUICHE patches for crash bugs in ``QuicSpdyStream`` ``OnDataAvailable()`` and ``OnInitialHeaderComplete()``.\n- area: quic\n  change: |\n    Fixed crash bug when QUIC downstream stream was read closed and then timed out.\n- area: tls\n  change: |\n    Fix a ``RELEASE_ASSERT`` when using :ref:`auto_sni <envoy_v3_api_field_config.core.v3.UpstreamHttpProtocolOptions.auto_sni>`\n    if the downstream request ``:authority`` was longer than 255 characters.\n- area: tracing\n  change: |\n    Fix an issue where span id is missing from OpenTelemetry access log entries.\n- area: ext_authz\n  change: |\n    Added field\n    :ref:`validate_mutations <envoy_v3_api_field_extensions.filters.http.ext_authz.v3.ExtAuthz.validate_mutations>`,\n    which, when set to ``true``, adds header and query parameter mutation validation to the HTTP ext_authz\n    filter. If an authz response contains invalid mutations, the filter responds to the downstream\n    request with HTTP ``500 Internal Server Error``. If you use ext_authz with an untrusted side stream,\n    it's recommended you set this to ``true``.\n- area: http\n  change: |\n    Fix a crash when reloading the HTTP Connection Manager via ECDS.\n- area: cares\n  change: |\n    Upgraded c-ares library to 1.20.1 and added fix to c-ares DNS implementation to additionally check for ``ARES_EREFUSED``,\n    ``ARES_ESERVFAIL`` and ``ARES_ENOTIMP`` status. This applies when\n    ``include_tls_session`` is ``true``. The requested server name is set on a connection when filters such as the TLS\n    inspector are used.\n- area: oauth\n  change: |\n    The ID token cookie now expires at the same time the id token itself expires, instead of when the access token expires.\n- area: decompression\n  change: |\n    Fixed a bug where Envoy will go into an endless loop when using the brotli decompressor. If the input stream has\n    redundant data, the decompressor will loop forever.\n- area: websocket\n  change: |\n    Only ``101`` is considered a successful response for websocket handshake for HTTP/1.1, and Envoy as a proxy will proxy the response\n    header from upstream to downstream and then close the request if other status is received. This behavior can be\n    reverted by ``envoy_reloadable_features_check_switch_protocol_websocket_handshake``.\n- area: async http client\n  change: |\n    Added one option to disable the response body buffering for mirror request.
